Shen Bao Amateur Weekly

Amateur Warm Talk

The So-Called Hirota's New Policy Toward China 285

— Han Ying

Bearing Hirota's new instructions, Japanese Minister to China, Ariyoshi, is about to leave Tokyo to return to his post. It is said that Ariyoshi's visit will be to earnestly entice us to directly resolve various pending issues, using the slogan of "coexistence and co-prosperity" to urge our economic cooperation with the Japanese puppet regime. It seems that the Sino-Japanese issue is about to enter a new phase. According to reports, Foreign Minister Hirota's recent policy toward China contains six points. Let us now list them and refute them one by one:

(1) Due to the April 17th statement, the Chinese side's feelings toward Japan have changed again, misunderstanding that Japan intends to invade China. After the minister returns to his post, he should explain that Japan's true intention is to maintain peace in the Far East and seek coexistence and co-prosperity between China and Japan, and urge the Chinese side to understand this policy.

Japan's April 17th statement has exposed its entire conspiracy against China, and its ambition to dominate East Asia has long been seen through by the world. Now Hirota claims that the true intention of the statement is to maintain peace in the Far East and seek coexistence and co-prosperity between China and Japan, urging our country to understand this policy. Isn't this a self-deceiving statement! May I ask how to maintain peace in the Far East? How to interpret coexistence and co-prosperity? If forcing other countries under one's own control is called maintaining peace in the Far East, and seizing other countries' lands as one's own is called coexistence and co-prosperity, then we really dare not accept it!

(2) Japan wants China to understand that Japan and "Manchukuo" jointly bear the responsibility for peace in East Asia. If China awakens and accepts Japan's sincerity, Japan will spare no effort to assist in the prosperity and unification of friendly China.

We have not been able to understand Japan's sincerity to this day, nor dare to accept it! We only feel that the responsibility for the lack of peace in East Asia should be borne by Japan. Because East Asia was originally very peaceful, it was only after Japan occupied the four northeastern provinces on September 18th that it showed signs of turmoil. As for the prosperity and unification of our country, Japan has already destroyed them completely, so we dare not accept assistance! We only hope that we will no longer be destroyed in the future, which is already fortunate!

(3) Japan is determined to oppose to the end any actions by third parties that contain the separation of the coexistence relationship between China and Japan. China should understand Japan's policy and promote political and economic harmony between China and Japan. For example, France's loan to the Zhengtai Railway, Japan believes is fair assistance to China. However, Japan believes that international technical cooperation will promote the opening of joint management, so it opposes it.

This article explains that Japan does not allow third parties to interfere with Japan's aggression against China and opposes any international assistance to China. Our country is an independent and sovereign country and also a member of the League of Nations, and has the right to request assistance from the League of Nations. It is not yet known whether technical cooperation will promote joint management. If there is really such a danger, then our attitude towards joint management, like towards dominance, is to vigorously resist it, without Japan worrying for us. Our country's economic cooperation with various countries, if it is aggressive, not only Japan, but any country will definitely reject it.

(4) Restore trade between China and Japan, complete the East Asian economic sphere with Japan as the leader, and make China understand that increasing trade between the two countries will increase the welfare of the people of both countries.

What is called the East Asian economic sphere? Who recognizes Japan as the leader? This is a bit incomprehensible. Increasing trade between the two countries is certainly beneficial to Japan, but harmful to us. What welfare can the people of our country have to speak of?

(5) Make the Chinese authorities understand that the restoration of China's rural bankruptcy can only be achieved through cooperation with Japan and "Manchukuo," vigorously advocating economic cooperation between China, Japan, and "Manchukuo," which can promote the prosperity of East Asia and can also use this to save its own financial circles, and urge Chinese politicians and their guiding classes to understand their responsibilities, in order to realize the plan of the Sino-Japanese-Manchukuo economic alliance.

The bankruptcy of China's rural areas is the result of excessive economic aggression by imperialists. To save this crisis, we must do our best to resist this aggression. Cooperation with Japan and "Manchukuo" will not only fail to restore its prosperity, but will only accelerate its collapse. The so-called Sino-Japanese-Manchukuo economic alliance plan, whose plan is this?

(6) China raises tariffs for financial reasons to prevent the dumping of Japanese goods. This policy hinders the prosperity of Japanese industries. Japan must advocate from the standpoint of the people that the use of cheap Japanese goods is beneficial to consumers, and persuade the Chinese authorities to revise tariffs to reduce the burden on Chinese consumers in order to promote the sale of Japanese goods.

Raising tariffs to prevent the dumping of Japanese goods is a policy that hinders the prosperity of Japanese industries, which is a fact. Because in this way, Japan's economic aggression cannot proceed smoothly. To overcome this obstacle, naturally, we must ask our country to revise tariffs. However, in the world, there has been no country that is willing to revise tariffs to allow foreign goods to be dumped. If it is said that this can reduce the burden on the people, then Japan can simply abolish tariffs and allow foreign goods to invade. Wouldn't the Japanese people be greatly benefited? What does Japan think? Who can accept such a request?

Overall, the six points raised by Japan are extremely unreasonable! Solving one or two hundred pending cases under these basic principles is really too early at this time! Unless the hearts of the people of the whole country are dead, I believe no one will accept it!

Life

Family Letter 286

— Jia Huan

Summer days are very long; the cotton mill hasn't blown the whistle yet, and it's already dawn.

The black manure carts enter the alley every day at this time. The iron wheels rolling on the concrete ground make a rumbling noise. Then: "Emptying the chamber pots!" A sharp, knife-like roar, replacing the whistle of the cotton mill, stabs the people in their sleep like a knife, suddenly causing a sting, waking them up. The alley is filled with a commotion. The landlady downstairs, perhaps because she is old and has neurasthenia, is easily startled. When that first sound of "Emptying the chamber pots!" comes from the entrance of the alley, it is followed by her shouting.

"Yuying, the chamber pot emptiers are here, hurry! Sister-in-law in the back building! The pavilion..." After calling her daughter-in-law, then the sister-in-law in the back building, the pavilion, she calls them in turn. This seems to have become a fixed task for her every morning. She is like a clock in this house, and the tenants living here won't be late if they get up according to her standard. The one who gets up earliest in this house is the sister-in-law in the back building; she always answers first when the landlady shouts.

"Thank you, good old lady! I'm up." It's this sentence every morning; the tone is so gentle that it makes people feel happy.

This morning, I don't know why, maybe she fell asleep; the landlady downstairs shouted once, twice, but the sister-in-law in the back building still didn't answer. The landlady's daughter-in-law had already gotten up, and the woman in the pavilion had also left. I could hear all of this clearly. Why hasn't she gotten up yet? Could she really be asleep? I felt a little worried for her, and couldn't stay still in bed. "Sister-in-law in the back building! The good old lady downstairs has called, aren't you getting up yet? It's getting late, if you don't get up, you'll be late for the factory!" I was afraid she had really forgotten and didn't remember to go to the factory, so I reached out and knocked on the wall a few times.

"Ah!... Thank you, Uncle! I, I'm not working anymore..." The voice of the sister-in-law in the back building was a bit trembling, as if she was about to cry.

"What? Not working anymore?" My heart skipped a beat; "Is there no work at the factory?" I asked anxiously.

There was no answer; but she really cried, and cried very sadly. I heard her crying so sadly, and knew that her work had really stopped. But she usually worked very diligently, and I had never seen her stop for a day; she was always the first to get up in this house every day, and had never been late. What could have caused her to be laid off made one think.

The sun quietly shone in, warming the floorboards of the room, and the heat gradually increased. It felt like countless ants were biting all over my body, and my skin felt like it was being pricked by needles. At this time, I remembered the crying of the sister-in-law in the back building again. There was a big knot in my heart, and I couldn't sleep no matter what.

I jumped out of bed and paced around the room aimlessly; I still felt the distress of losing something valuable, like I couldn't find it for a while.

"Bang," "Bang"! Uncle in the front building!" Wasn't that the sister-in-law in the back building knocking on the door? I was suddenly startled and went to open the door.

"Uncle! I want to ask you a favor, would you be willing?" She smiled reluctantly; her eyelids were still red.

"Is it writing a letter? Yes, yes." I saw that she had a few sheets of paper and envelopes in her hand and quickly agreed. "Thank you! Really, I'm always troubling you, I'm embarrassed..." A slight blush appeared on her face, and she was afraid that I would see her shy appearance, so she quickly wiped her eyes with a handkerchief. "It's nothing, we live in the same house, why be so polite? Are you writing to Hankou? I know that the only one she communicates with is her husband; but I ask her like this, it seems to have become a habit, every time I write a letter for her, it's always like this.

"Yes!"

"What are you going to say in the letter? Wasn't it not long ago" that you wrote a letter? You communicate once every few days. Unmarried couples aren't as diligent as you two!" I joked with her, and she couldn't help but laugh. She said, "Uncle in the front building is really starting to joke; other people here almost don't have any food to eat, what's there to talk about being good?" She frowned tightly and took a slight breath.

"No food to eat? You're being too polite." I showed a distrustful look.

"Really, what's there to be polite about? Please write this for me: say that I'm not working at the factory anymore, and now I want to go back, tell him to send me some money quickly for travel expenses. I don't want to live in Shanghai anymore, there's no room for us to live in Shanghai, even if I have strength, I can't sell it for money: I'd rather go back to the countryside, even if I use up all my strength, it's much more comfortable than selling my strength for money in Shanghai and having to look at people's faces..." Her throat was a bit stiff again, like it was in the morning; her face was deathly pale, and beads of sweat the size of beans were dripping from her forehead, as if she had been drenched by a rainstorm. I wrote according to what she said, and when she finished speaking, I put down the pen.

"Is there anything else?" I said, "Aren't you going to tell him about how you came out of the factory?"

"Yes, I want to tell him: but if I write too much, won't you be tired?" She looked at me and smiled, seeming very apologetic. "It's okay, what's it to write a letter." I said confidently.

"Then, thank you!" She smiled again and continued, "I came out yesterday; I worked a total of twelve days this month and got three yuan and eight jiao of wages!!"

"What, twelve days only three yuan and eight jiao?" I interrupted her. "Yes! This is already considered good!" She said with a sigh. "At least tell him to send ten yuan, otherwise I won't be able to leave. There's no way around it, it's not that I'm unwilling to work hard; the reason is that the foreman has his own people and doesn't have a place to put them, so he's using us to open the knife..."

"He must have given some reason, right? He can't fire you for no reason if you didn't do anything wrong?" I began to doubt her words.

"Want a reason? That's very easy. His mouth is big, our mouths are small, his reasons are always right; he can find bones in an egg, what's so difficult about finding fault with workers?" She opened her eyes wide, looking at me with a very experienced look.

"Yes, this is their specialty; but what exactly did he find that was wrong with you to fire you?" I asked immediately.

"Listen! Listen and write it down as I say." She handed over another piece of paper, "Our kind of glass grinding work is simply like being a mason; all day long, our whole bodies are immersed in mud to make a living. That sand table, like a train executioner, turns along with the 'motor'; the water tank is hanging in the air, and the mud invades the tank and flows onto the sand table with the water. The wind power stirred up by the water and sand table sprinkles onto everyone like a rainstorm, and our whole bodies are covered with layers of mud, like falling in the mud on a dirt road in the countryside, and you can't even see your face when you get up. The nature of glass cups is very fragile, and if they touch uneven mouths, they easily break..." She took a glass cup to show me

Page 22

, afraid that I didn't quite understand what she was saying. She continued: "At this time, if you are not careful, your own hand will suffer the same fate as the glass cup. It doesn't matter if your hand is cut at this time, no one will ask; however, at the same time, if you hear the sound of a glass cup breaking, the foreman will immediately rush over and scold you wildly with wide eyes. Don't I have many cuts on my hands? But because of these many marks, I have seen countless faces and heard countless curses!

Yesterday, the mouth grinder suddenly broke down; the foreman looked at the thousands of dozens of cups, feeling the anger of having no solution, jumping like a chicken in the water. 'Dead people! You don't know the machine is about to break, are you acting like someone who works? Rice buckets!' The worker at the mouth grinder listened to him scolding, standing there like a statue, staring at the broken machine; sweat was flowing down his face like rain, as if it were rivers drawn on a map. 'What are you standing here for? Are you waiting to be invited, huh?' The foreman grabbed the arm of the mouth grinder and pushed him forward. He woke up as if he had had a nightmare, and his body leaned forward, almost falling like a starving dog licking shit; the other workers laughed when they saw it. He finally fixed the problem with the machine; the foreman's steel-blue face faded a little.

The mouth grinder is not a coppersmith after all, although he barely repaired the machine, the cups that were ground out were not as neat as before. Thousands of dozens of cups were all like dog teeth, and when they were put on the grinding machine—sand table—they cracked and shattered. The foreman's two eyeballs were like man-eating monsters, staring with a pose of choosing someone to devour, his eyes turning on everyone's faces; at this time, judging everyone's final fate. Snap! A cup in my hand shattered; my heart jumped, and I stared at the sand table with my face burning, hating that it had to go against me at this time. At this time, the foreman's eyes were exploding with red veins as if they had been burned, he walked over and looked at me with a sneer; he said fiercely: 'If you can't grind it well, don't grind it; if everyone is like you and wastes cups, then why should this factory stay open? You probably don't want to do this dirty thing either, I know. You'd better go back and enjoy yourself, we don't need you here either; go to the accounting room to calculate your wages.' He quickly wrote the paper for taking wages and gave it to me, and walked away with a stern face. I didn't argue with him at all, but there was nothing to argue about; his mouth is big, and the reasons he says are always right. I took the wages and walked out, and I felt a lot lighter in my heart..." Her face was even more pale, like wax, and her chest was heaving, showing that she had difficulty breathing, as if she was hiding a lot of unspeakable pain in her heart; but on the surface, she pretended to be indifferent, her lips flickered slightly, and she let out a wry smile. "That's right, it's not good to go to another factory in this factory, can't I still sell my strength if I have it?" I knew that these words could not grasp her pain, but I couldn't find any more appropriate and considerate words to comfort her; what she needed at this time was not words, even if you spoke as moving and beautiful as a oriole, you couldn't fill the actual emptiness in her stomach.

"Um!" She smiled bitterly. Experience told her that this was my forced comfort; "Shanghai doesn't have my life; isn't every factory the same as this one?" "Don't be an official if you have no one in the court," people like me who are lonely will suffer the same fate wherever they go!! Thank you, Uncle! I'm sorry for troubling you to write for so long, really..." She stood up reluctantly with a sad look and said a few polite words to me and left.

I looked at her back and felt a surge of sympathetic sadness. "Ah! Poor woman!" Gently floated out of my mouth.

Miscellaneous Works

Although a Small Vendor, He Can Support Himself Without Anyone's Pity. His Arrogant Spirit Is Innate, With No Notion of Depression or Injustice. The Transformation of the Eccentric Old Man Ding. 287

— Xinglin

I remember a certain great writer once said: "Has anyone ever fallen from a well-to-do family into poverty? I think that on this road, one can see the true face of the world." The two paths of wealth and poverty isolate people, and after a transformation, one's physique and the warmth and coldness of the world will be tested. This is not wrong at all.

In Tianjin, there is an old man Ding who sells tangdui (that is, hawthorn fruit dipped in rock sugar, skewered with bamboo sticks, called "tangqiu" in the South and "tanghulu" in the North). When he was rich, he spent money like dirt. When he was poor, he supported himself without anyone's pity. He was playful and cynical, but his innate arrogance is worthy of admiration and infatuation.

Lin Moqing once wrote a short biography for him, saying: "Ding Ziboyu, people respectfully call him Old Man Ding, is a son of a prominent family in Tianjin."

His family used to have a customs office job, what Tianjin people call a big customs house. Most of the prominent families in the town were relatives. Boyu was born with luxurious surroundings, and his clothing, food, and entertainment were all he could ask for. When he went out, he was carried in a sedan chair with attendants, just like a noble official." Reading this passage, one can see a rough outline of his life. At the age of sixteen, he inherited his father's business and "entered the customs" to work, but he did not get rid of his extravagant habits. It is said that he smoked opium. When he was about to go out, the doorman would call the sedan carriers to wait, but the sedan carriers would also be lying on the couch, not yet satisfied with their opium addiction. He was not anxious, but laughed and scolded, and stood in front of the door to wait. It can be seen that Old Man Ding had a broad mind and a generous demeanor, putting himself in other people's shoes and being able to understand the suffering of the sedan carriers. His four sedan carriers all wore gray squirrel mandarin jackets turned inside out in winter. From this alone, one can imagine his luxury in those years.

He was originally a childlike person full of interest, often looking for novel things to amuse himself. When the bicycle invented by Westerners was first discovered in Tianjin, all the riders were Westerners. He immediately bought one, and his control was very skilled. Ding was the first Chinese person in Tianjin to be able to ride a bicycle. He also held hundreds of strings of money and bought dozens of pounds of sugar. In the living room, he placed a stove, a copper pot, a stone slab, and other things to learn how to make tangdui. He originally did it for entertainment, but unexpectedly, he later used this profession to support himself. His short biography also says: "When the Boxer Rebellion broke out, the family was burned and looted, and the customs office was cut down. He went from being very rich to being penniless, but he refused to borrow money. Even if relatives and friends pitied him and helped him, he would refuse. He only made various kinds of sugar food, carrying a basket and selling it along the street. His family of eight relied on this for more than twenty years."

The tanghulu he made was famous for its excellent quality. First, because he had fallen from being a son of a rich family to a small vendor, he did not covet heavy profits. Second, because the things he made were very exquisite and indeed delicious. It is said that he had unique characteristics in the work of boiling sugar and dipping fruit. The tanghulu he made was crystal clear and crispy, could be placed in ashes without getting dirty, and could be placed in his arms without sticking. The sales were very wide, earning three or two yuan a day, more than enough to make a living, and he was leisurely and content. He never felt any emotion or depression about the rise and fall of his fortunes. The reason why Ding is called an eccentric is actually due to this.

When I was in Tianjin, I heard his name and spent two days trying to meet him, but I never succeeded.

Old Man Ding died in 1929 at the age of fifty-seven. He had no children and his old wife died first. Once, he was carrying a basket into the market, selling loudly, and accidentally met his relative in the West Jieyuan area. The relative pitied his downfall and wanted to give him money to persuade him to change his profession, but Ding refused angrily and said, "This business cannot be done, what kind of industry can be done? You think selling tangdui is base, but I think opening a pawn shop or setting up a jewelry store is not necessarily noble." After saying this, he angrily waved his sleeves and left, while the relative was greatly disappointed. In the eyes of others, they all thought that he was in a bad mood, but in my opinion, it was really a famous and true saying.

Another time, he met a friend in the North Daguan area. That person was afraid that he would be embarrassed, so he deliberately turned his head to avoid him, but he caught up and stopped the person, laughing and saying, "You still owe me money. Don't avoid me, I didn't ask you for it!"

Art World

Emerging from "Street Movie Theaters" 288

— Li Qing

On the open space at the bend of Beijing Road, a large canvas tent, underneath which sits a semi-circular wooden cabinet, a homemade film projector, and a pitifully old small motor—this constitutes a "street movie theater."

"Shasha, didi dang, shasha, didi dang..." the small motor gasps for breath.

"Four copper coins for a look, do you want to see the Righteous Volunteers fighting the Japanese..." This is the mobile advertisement.

Page 23

The person sitting there winding the film shouts desperately.

The audience here isn't the young mistresses and wives seeking pleasure outside, nor the gentlemen with top hats and "walking sticks," or the well-dressed young men and women holding hands. The audience here is the ordinary masses, dressed untidily but with thick arms. They work all year round, their lives are too bitter. During this only holiday, they want to have some fun, they want to seek some comfort, so they spend four copper coins to watch a movie because they can't afford the movie theater.

After paying four copper coins, I was also led to the front of a hole, sitting on a bench about three inches wide. The person who brought me pulled the string that struck the copper coins. The cloth covering the hole was then pulled up. Thus, the situation inside the wooden cabinet was fully reflected in my eyes. Inside the cabinet, there was a small screen, and nothing else. On the outside of the cabinet, there were more than a dozen holes, which were for the audience to watch the show.

I watched a short film about the Righteous Volunteers fighting the Japanese army. There was no main character, the main characters were the "Righteous Volunteers" and the "Japanese army." The plot was very simple. The Japanese army used cannons and machine guns to attack the Righteous Volunteers, and the Righteous Volunteers were defeated. But the Righteous Volunteers had spears and broadswords, and a lot of people, so they counterattacked and finally defeated the Japanese army, and that was the end. Although the film was so simple, projected so vaguely and unclearly, and the small motor kept "shasha, didi dang..." shouting, many people watched it with great interest. When the Righteous Volunteers counterattacked, some people even shouted. After the film was over, some people cursed, wanting to "fuck" the Japanese people's "eighteenth generation ancestors"... From this, I realized the effect of this kind of film.

I couldn't help but think of the current movies. What are the current movies like? Let me go and inspect them.

As long as you walk past the entrance of a movie theater, the electric poles, the red lights, the large advertisements... they will catch your attention; but when you see clearly, you will always see words like "sensual blockbuster," "extremely hot," "fleshly," "voluptuous breasts," "snowy legs," etc. This kind of movie has completely become a pastime for young ladies and young masters. Our "artists" who are "art for art's sake" have "artified" everything... to relieve the boredom of young ladies and young masters. Our "artists" don't care about anything. In order to please the young masters and young ladies, even if they distort the facts, they don't care.

What's the use of such movies?

Although recently there are said to be many relatively "progressive" films (but they still inevitably play the role of embellishment and distortion), it doesn't solve the problem. For example, in this time of national crisis, the most urgent issue for us is how to fight for national liberation and independence. This is certainly not a matter for a small number of young masters and young ladies, but requires the people of the whole country to rise up and do it. Can the current movies shoulder this responsibility of propaganda and mobilization? Moreover, even if there are good films, they cannot reach the general public at present. On the surface, theaters seem to be very casual places, where anyone has the opportunity to enter; but in reality? In fact, movie theaters have signs that say "no money, no entry." So, how can the current movies achieve the task of reaching the masses?

Since seeing this "street movie theater," it made me think of the issue of "popularizing movies"; this naturally refers not only to the content of the film, but also to the form—the form of performance is included, that is to say, making it possible for everyone to see it.

Scientific Miscellany

Wheel-less Spherical Train 289

— Yi Qi

I once saw a new type of train in a magazine, which was said to be the fastest and most unique in style, but unfortunately, it didn't tell us what it was all about.

Later, I heard people say that this is a train without wheels, which is even stranger. A train without wheels is like a fish without fins, a bird without wings, and a horse without legs, isn't it?

But this was the view of two or three years ago. Now, it has gone from theory to complete realization. From Moscow to Noginsk, there is such a train called "spherical train," its number is "SH-4-", and it officially started "carrying various goods" this year.

The model of this "spherical train" was first trialed in Yarmolchuk, a few kilometers away from Moscow. It can let you take a ride, and it will surprise you when it starts moving. Its speed and turning ability are not comparable to ordinary trains. Its track is trough-shaped, twelve centimeters wide, and made of the most rigid concrete.

The train itself is an interesting combination of bicycle, tram, and mine. The cigar shape of the train is best to reduce air resistance and achieve its maximum speed.

Under the train, there are two large spheres, one in front and one in the back, which are exceptionally smooth. When turning, it sways to one side like a rocking boat. If you are riding for the first time, this kind of turning will surprise you, thinking that the train has overturned.

The speed of this train is 250 to 300 kilometers per hour, four or five times faster than the fastest express train.

The Soviet Union is a vast and resource-rich country. It takes a very long time to travel from City A to City B. With this train, the time will certainly be shortened, calculated not in days but in hours. For example, a person living 150 to 200 kilometers away from Moscow can very well go to Moscow to see a night show and go back to sleep at the same time as usual. This is not just imagination!

This spherical train will overcome distance and time!

Overseas Correspondence Network

Coolies 290

— Yi Jun

North Borneo Correspondence

North Borneo (Nord Borneo-insulae) is also known as Borneo by some and is a British Malayan colony. Its largest seaport is Sandakan, followed by Api and Douou. Timber is the largest product, followed by rubber, betel nuts, coconuts, salted fish, and fruits. Every year, no less than 18,000 "coolies" (meaning laborers, slaves) are shipped in from China. The majority are forced into the mountains to cut timber and collect rubber. They work over ten hours a day, and their labor is compensated at only ten yuan or so a month, and they must also endure multiple layers of exploitation by the coolie heads (foremen). Due to the dry climate and the hardship of life, as well as the mountain mists, miasma, wild beasts, and poisonous snakes in the mountains, deaths are reported daily (the so-called dead coolies). In reality, once they are forced into the mountains, even if they have great abilities, they have no hope of returning to their homeland. They can only remotely yearn for the shadow of their homeland across the sea. Fate is decided: a coolie for life, a slave for life, until death.

In the mountains, the coolie heads—the foreign capitalists' trained dogs—are very clever. Every dusk and night, they open their opium dens, fan-tan games, pai gow games, bullfighting... attracting a large number of coolies to gather. They say this is to regulate the workers' monotonous lives. Opium can be bought on credit, and even gambling money can be borrowed. Their opium and gambling businesses are very advantageous, even if the "mata" (police) come, it doesn't matter, because the coolie heads have already obtained permission from the bosses (British). More precisely, the mata have received "usage" fees.

Sunday is usually a day of rest, the day when the coolie heads' wealth flows in, the day when their opium dens and gambling houses have the best business. But some workers will also take a small steamer to go to Sandakan for a while, or go to a brothel once, to regulate their sexual monotony. But it costs at least ten dollars. If the coolie head is willing to guarantee credit, that is also possible.

Sandakan is a so-called largest seaport in North Borneo, the necessary entrance to all the mountains, and the general gateway for transportation to various ports. There are often two ships coming here from Hong Kong—Jardine Matheson's Siu Sang and Mau Sang. Other ships from Singapore, Little Luzon, and some unbranded ships arrive every month. Imports are some groceries, and exports are timber, coconuts, rubber, fruits... Sandakan looks like a village on the outside. The majority of residents are Malay natives and Chinese. In terms of transportation, there are no trams or rickshaws on land, only a few cars for government British officials to ride in. Water transportation is all dugout canoes and longboats, which transport goods, and there are only two sand boats that carry people, rowed by Cantonese Tanka girls. The post office is a small wooden house made of wooden frames. All recipients must personally inquire whether they have a letter and personally pick it up because the post office does not have mailmen. There is one main road and three side streets. Most of the shops are opened by Chinese, and some are opened by Malays. The largest Chinese shop is Wan Ho Yuen Trading Company, said to have several million in capital. There is also a Sai Shing Gold Shop opened by Chinese. The next are food halls, tea houses, grocery stores, opium dens, a large gambling house, and sixteen Chinese brothels, one Japanese-run Shimizu Imperial, one Japanese-run Shimizu Imperial Cuisine, and one Japanese brothel with the large letters Z0.3 written on it. In this respect, Sandakan really has some of the flavor of Monte Carlo. The Chinese residing in Sandakan, apart from some staff, shopkeepers, and prostitutes, are those "gamblers" and some so-called "big hats" (wealthy people). Gamblers make a living by gambling, and they must have capital on hand to do so. The so-called big hats refer to those rich people, such as shop owners, brothel pimps, owners of large gambling houses, and even coolie heads are included. Sandakan's economic authority is entirely in their hands. As for Sandakan's administrative power, it is in the hands of the Governor of North Borneo and the local government, which are composed of British people. The government has a Chinese Affairs Secretary, who specializes in handling all Chinese affairs, and the director is also a British person. The Chinese also have an authoritative Lin Min Ding (Wen Cheng), who is a local gentleman, a high-ranking Chinese, and the Chinese in Sandakan, North Borneo, treat him like a consul. The situation of the Chinese community in North Borneo is roughly like this.

International Broadcasting Radio Station

Soviet Orchards 291

— Shu Sheng

The completion of the First Five-Year Plan can be proven by the development of the fruit tree industry. Replacing those small orchards scattered around, mostly planted with old-fashioned methods, the world's largest, specialized orchards with modern machinery have now been established. For example, the "Giant" orchard covers 2,400 hectares, the Eskine State Orchard covers 2,600 hectares, the Rebedin Orchard covers 2,400 hectares, the Diyemaiti Vineyard covers 1,900 hectares, etc.—these large areas are all planted using specialized methods.

Continued on page five.

Home
